   105|         1|  1.04904e-05|  1.04904e-05|  0.00%|    """Profiler class.
   106|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|
   107|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    self.cur is always a tuple.  Each such tuple corresponds to a stack
   108|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    frame that is currently active (self.cur[-2]).  The following are the
   109|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    definitions of its members.  We use this external "parallel stack" to
   110|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    avoid contaminating the program that we are profiling. (old profiler
   111|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    used to write into the frames local dictionary!!) Derived classes
   112|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    can change the definition of some entries, as long as they leave
   113|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    [-2:] intact (frame and previous tuple).  In case an internal error is
   114|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    detected, the -3 element is used as the function name.
   115|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|
   116|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    [ 0] = Time that needs to be charged to the parent frame's function.
   117|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|           It is used so that a function call will not have to access the
   118|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|           timing data for the parent frame.
   119|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    [ 1] = Total time spent in this frame's function, excluding time in
   120|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|           subfunctions (this latter is tallied in cur[2]).
   121|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    [ 2] = Total time spent in subfunctions, excluding time executing the
   122|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|           frame's function (this latter is tallied in cur[1]).
   123|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    [-3] = Name of the function that corresponds to this frame.
   124|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    [-2] = Actual frame that we correspond to (used to sync exception handling).
   125|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    [-1] = Our parent 6-tuple (corresponds to frame.f_back).
   126|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|
   127|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    Timing data for each function is stored as a 5-tuple in the dictionary
   128|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    self.timings[].  The index is always the name stored in self.cur[-3].
   129|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    The following are the definitions of the members:
   130|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|
   131|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    [0] = The number of times this function was called, not counting direct
   132|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|          or indirect recursion,
   133|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    [1] = Number of times this function appears on the stack, minus one
   134|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    [2] = Total time spent internal to this function
   135|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    [3] = Cumulative time that this function was present on the stack.  In
   136|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|          non-recursive functions, this is the total execution time from start
   137|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|          to finish of each invocation of a function, including time spent in

   185|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        timer = self.timer
   186|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        t = timer()
   187|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        t = t[0] + t[1] - self.t - self.bias

   189|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        if event == "c_call":

   191|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|

   243|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # In the event handlers, the first 3 elements of self.cur are unpacked
   244|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # into vrbls w/ 3-letter names.  The last two characters are meant to be
   245|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # mnemonic:

   439|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    #******************************************************************
   440|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # The following calculates the overhead for using a profiler.  The
   441|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # problem is that it takes a fair amount of time for the profiler
   442|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # to stop the stopwatch (from the time it receives an event).
   443|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # Similarly, there is a delay from the time that the profiler
   444|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # re-starts the stopwatch before the user's code really gets to
   445|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # continue.  The following code tries to measure the difference on
   446|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # a per-event basis.
   447|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    #
   448|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # Note that this difference is only significant if there are a lot of
   449|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # events, and relatively little user code per event.  For example,
   450|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # code with small functions will typically benefit from having the
   451|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # profiler calibrated for the current platform.  This *could* be
   452|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # done on the fly during init() time, but it is not worth the
   453|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # effort.  Also note that if too large a value specified, then
   454|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # execution time on some functions will actually appear as a
   455|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # negative number.  It is *normal* for some functions (with very
   456|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # low call counts) to have such negative stats, even if the
   457|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # calibration figure is "correct."
   458|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    #
   459|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # One alternative to profile-time calibration adjustments (i.e.,
   460|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # adding in the magic little delta during each event) is to track
   461|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # more carefully the number of events (and cumulatively, the number
   462|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # of events during sub functions) that are seen.  If this were
   463|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # done, then the arithmetic could be done after the fact (i.e., at
   464|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # display time).  Currently, we track only call/return events.
   465|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # These values can be deduced by examining the callees and callers
   466|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # vectors for each functions.  Hence we *can* almost correct the
   467|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # internal time figure at print time (note that we currently don't
   468|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # track exception event processing counts).  Unfortunately, there
   469|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # is currently no similar information for cumulative sub-function
   470|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # time.  It would not be hard to "get all this info" at profiler
   471|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # time.  Specifically, we would have to extend the tuples to keep
   472|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # counts of this in each frame, and then extend the defs of timing
   473|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # tuples to include the significant two figures. I'm a bit fearful
   474|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # that this additional feature will slow the heavily optimized
   475|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # event/time ratio (i.e., the profiler would run slower, fur a very
   476|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    # low "value added" feature.)
   477|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|    #**************************************************************
   478|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|
   479|         1|  1.69277e-05|  1.69277e-05|  0.00%|    def calibrate(self, m, verbose=0):
   480|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        if self.__class__ is not Profile:
   481|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|            raise TypeError("Subclasses must override .calibrate().")
   482|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|
   483|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        saved_bias = self.bias
   484|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        self.bias = 0
   485|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        try:
   486|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|            return self._calibrate_inner(m, verbose)
   487|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        finally:
   488|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|            self.bias = saved_bias
   489|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|
   490|         1|  2.00272e-05|  2.00272e-05|  0.00%|    def _calibrate_inner(self, m, verbose):
   491|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        get_time = self.get_time
   492|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|
   493|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        # Set up a test case to be run with and without profiling.  Include
   494|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        # lots of calls, because we're trying to quantify stopwatch overhead.
   495|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        # Do not raise any exceptions, though, because we want to know
   496|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        # exactly how many profile events are generated (one call event, +
   497|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        # one return event, per Python-level call).
   498|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|
   499|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        def f1(n):
   500|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|            for i in range(n):
   501|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|                x = 1
   502|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|
   503|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        def f(m, f1=f1):
   504|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|            for i in range(m):
   505|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|                f1(100)
   506|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|

   508|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|

   511|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        f(m)
   512|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        t1 = get_time()
   513|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        elapsed_noprofile = t1 - t0
   514|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        if verbose:
   515|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|            print("elapsed time without profiling =", elapsed_noprofile)
   516|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|
   517|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        # elapsed_profile <- time f(m) takes with profiling.  The difference
   518|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        # is profiling overhead, only some of which the profiler subtracts
   519|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        # out on its own.
   520|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        p = Profile()
   521|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        t0 = get_time()
   522|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        p.runctx('f(m)', globals(), locals())
   523|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        t1 = get_time()
   524|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        elapsed_profile = t1 - t0
   525|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        if verbose:
   526|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|            print("elapsed time with profiling =", elapsed_profile)
   527|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|
   528|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        # reported_time <- "CPU seconds" the profiler charged to f and f1.
   529|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        total_calls = 0.0
   530|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        reported_time = 0.0
   531|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        for (filename, line, funcname), (cc, ns, tt, ct, callers) in \
   532|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|                p.timings.items():
   533|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|            if funcname in ("f", "f1"):
   534|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|                total_calls += cc
   535|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|                reported_time += tt
   536|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|

   538|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|            print("'CPU seconds' profiler reported =", reported_time)
   539|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|            print("total # calls =", total_calls)
   540|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        if total_calls != m + 1:
   541|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|            raise ValueError("internal error: total calls = %d" % total_calls)
   542|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|
   543|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        # reported_time - elapsed_noprofile = overhead the profiler wasn't
   544|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        # able to measure.  Divide by twice the number of calls (since there
   545|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        # are two profiler events per call in this test) to get the hidden
   546|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        # overhead per event.
   547|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        mean = (reported_time - elapsed_noprofile) / 2.0 / total_calls
   548|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        if verbose:
   549|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|            print("mean stopwatch overhead per profile event =", mean)

   196|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        from the result vector and report these.  However, this is not
   197|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        very useful.  In a typical case, the lowest value gives a

   214|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|
   215|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        Calls the timeit method with increasing numbers from the sequence
   216|         0|            0|            0|  0.00%|        1, 2, 5, 10, 20, 50, ... until the time taken is at least 0.2
